The Thirty-Second Question: On the Infallibility of the Prophets, may God's blessings and peace be upon them. Know that disagreement in this matter occurs in four areas: First: What pertains to belief. The community is agreed that they are protected from disbelief and innovation, except for the Fadliyya of the Khawarij who permit disbelief upon the prophets — may God's blessings and peace be upon them — because according to them sin may issue from them, and every sin is disbelief according to them, and by this way they permitted disbelief from them. As for the Rawafid, they permit them to show the word of disbelief by way of taqiyya. Second: What pertains to the delivery of the laws and rulings from God Most High. The community is agreed that it is not permissible for them to distort or betray in this matter, neither deliberately nor inadvertently, otherwise no reliance would remain on any of the laws. Third: What pertains to fatwa. The community is agreed that deliberate error is not permissible; as for inadvertent error, they have differed on it. Fourth: What pertains to their actions and states. The community has differed on this into five schools: The first: the saying of the Hashwiyya, that it is permissible for them to commit major and minor sins. The second: that deliberate major sin is absolutely not permissible from them; as for deliberate minor sin, it is permissible on condition that it is not repulsive. But if deliberate minor sin is repulsive, then it is not permissible for them — like cheating in weights concerning less than a grain — and this is the saying of most Mu'tazila. The third: that deliberate major and minor sin are not permissible from them, but the commission of sin is permissible by way of error in interpretation, and this is the saying of al-Jubba'i. The fourth: that major and minor sin are not permissible, neither deliberately nor by erroneous interpretation. As for...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the disagreements regarding the infallibility ('isma) of the prophets. Razi introduces the thirty-second question and states that the disagreement occurs in four areas (mawādi'). The first area is belief (i'tiqād): the community (umma) agrees that prophets are protected from kufr (disbelief) and bid'a (innovation), except for the Fadliyya of the Khawarij, who allow kufr because for them every sin is kufr, and the Rawafid (Shi'a), who allow outward display of kufr under taqiyya (dissimulation). The second area is the delivery (tablīgh) of divine laws and rulings: the umma agrees that prophets cannot deliberately or inadvertently distort or betray, otherwise no certainty remains in the laws. The third area is fatwa (issuing legal opinions): the umma agrees that deliberate error is not permitted, but they differ on inadvertent error. The fourth area is their actions and states (af'āl wa aḥwāl): the umma has differed into five schools (madhāhib). Razi then lists the first four schools: 1) The Hashwiyya hold that prophets may commit both major and minor sins. 2) Most Mu'tazila hold that deliberate major sin is absolutely not permitted, but deliberate minor sin is permitted if it is not repulsive (e.g., cheating in weights below a grain); if repulsive, it is not permitted. 3) al-Jubba'i holds that deliberate major and minor sins are not permitted, but sin may occur by error in interpretation (ta'wil). 4) The fourth school, which appears to be the preferred view, holds that neither major nor minor sins occur from prophets, neither deliberately nor by erroneous interpretation. The text is cut off before the fifth school is described.

المعتزلة
الجبائي
الصغيرة

التأويل
التطفيف
المنفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila allow all minor sins from prophets.
Correction: The Mu'tazila only allow deliberate minor sins that are not repulsive (like cheating below a grain), and they forbid repulsive minor sins altogether.

Checkpoint
Which school allows prophets to commit major sins?
A) Hashwiyya
B) Most Mu'tazila
C) Al-Jubba'i
D) The fourth school

Key Takeaway
The first four schools on prophetic actions range from allowing all sins (Hashwiyya) to forbidding them completely (fourth school), with intermediate positions on minor sins and error in interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these four views do you find most compelling, and what does your choice reveal about how you view the prophets' relationship with Allah? Are you comfortable with any level of imperfection in those who deliver Allah's message?
?
Al-Jubba'i allows sin by error in interpretation. Have you ever excused your own wrong actions by claiming you 'didn't understand' or 'misinterpreted' a situation? How does that compare to the standard you hold for prophets?
?
The Hashwiyya claim that prophets can commit major sins. If you heard someone today say that about a beloved prophet, how would it make you feel? Does that reaction come from your faith or your personal attachment? How can you ground your reverence in scripture rather than emotion?

First Area: Infallibility in Belief
Razi states the consensus on infallibility in belief and cites two sectarian exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first area of disagreement concerning prophetic infallibility—belief—and the exceptions raised by the Khawarij and Rafidites.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible in belief, but two sects dissent with extreme views.

Razi begins by outlining four areas of debate on prophetic infallibility. The first area concerns belief: the consensus is that prophets are protected from disbelief and innovation, yet two sects—the Fudaliyya Khawarij and the Rafidites—hold deviant views. Let's examine these exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice how Razi states the consensus and then presents the exceptions.
The passage uses 'إلا' to introduce exceptions.
2
Identify the consensus and exceptions
Find the consensus (أجمعت الأمة) and the two exceptional groups. Understand their reasoning as given by Razi.
The Khawarij consider every sin as disbelief; the Rafidites permit outward denial under duress.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these exceptions matter for the doctrine of prophetic infallibility. How do they contrast with the mainstream view?
This area shows that even basic beliefs about prophets have been contested.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية والثلاثون في عصمة الأنبياء صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم اعلم أن الاختلاف في هذه المسألة واقع في أربعة مواضع: الأول : ما يتعلق بالاعتقاد وأجمعت الأمة على أنهم معصومون عن الكفر والبدعة، إلا الفضلية من الخوارج فإنهم يجوزون الكفر على الأنبياء - صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم - وذلك لأن عندهم يجوز صدور الذنب عنهم، وكل ذنب فهو كفر عندهم، وبهذا الطريق جوزوا صدور الكفر عنهم، وأما الروافض فإنهم يجوزون عليهم إظهار كلمة الكفر على سبيل التقية. الثاني : ما يتعلق بتبليغ الشرائع والأحكام من الله تعالى : وأجمعت الأمة على أنه لا يجوز عليهم التحريف والخيانة في هذا الباب لا بالعمد ولا بالسهو، وإلا لم يبق الاعتماد على شيء من الشرائع.
The Second and Thirty-First Issue: On the Infallibility of the Prophets, may God's blessings and peace be upon them. Know that disagreement concerning this issue occurs in four areas: First: What pertains to belief. The community has agreed that they are infallible from disbelief and innovation, except for the Fudaliyya among the Khawarij, for they permit disbelief upon the prophets—may God's blessings and peace be upon them—because in their view, the commission of sin is permissible from them, and every sin in their view is disbelief, and through this way they permit the occurrence of disbelief from them. As for the Rafidites, they permit them to display the word of disbelief for the sake of dissimulation. Second: What pertains to conveying the divine laws and rulings from God Almighty. The community has agreed that it is not permissible for them to commit distortion or betrayal in this matter, neither intentionally nor by forgetfulness, otherwise trust would not remain in any of the divine laws.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage classifies the first two areas of disagreement concerning prophetic infallibility. Razi begins by stating that the issue of infallibility is debated in four areas. The first area is belief: the community agrees that prophets are infallible from disbelief and innovation, except the Fudaliyya sect of the Khawarij, who permit prophets to commit disbelief because they believe any sin is disbelief. The Rafidites also permit prophets to outwardly utter disbelief under dissimulation. The second area is conveying divine laws: here there is consensus that prophets cannot distort or betray God's message, whether intentionally or by forgetfulness, as that would undermine all revealed law.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Muslims agree that prophets are completely infallible in belief without any exceptions.
Correction: While the majority holds this view, the Fudaliyya Khawarij and Rafidites present differing opinions as detailed by Razi.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Khawarij equated every sin with disbelief. Do you ever find yourself judging others' sins as if they negate their entire faith? How does this passage call you to examine the severity of your judgments?

Second Area: Infallibility in Conveying Divine Laws
Razi affirms the consensus that prophets are immune from distortion in conveying divine laws.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second area of disagreement—conveying divine laws—and the consensus that prophets cannot distort or betray the message.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible in delivering God's laws; distortion would destroy all trust in revelation.

After discussing belief, Razi turns to the second area: the transmission of divine laws. Here there is unanimity that prophets cannot intentionally or unintentionally alter the message. This lesson examines that consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the second area. Notice how Razi presents the consensus and its rationale.
The passage is concise but carries a strong logical consequence.
2
Identify the consensus and its scope
The consensus covers both intentional and unintentional distortion. Why does Razi mention both?
Prophetic mission requires complete trustworthiness without any possibility of error.
3
Analyze the consequence
Razi says if distortion were possible, no trust would remain in any divine law. Reflect on why this is a necessary conclusion.
This shows the foundational importance of this infallibility.

Third and Fourth Areas: Fatwa and Actions with Five Schools
Razi enumerates the third and fourth areas with five schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five schools of thought on the possibility of sins for prophets in their actions and the rule on intentional error in fatwa.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot intentionally err in fatwa; actions are debated across five schools.

Razi continues the discussion of prophetic infallibility by examining the remaining two areas: fatwa and actions. While there is consensus that a prophet cannot intentionally err in giving a legal ruling, the issue of forgetfulness is disputed. Regarding actions, the community splits into five distinct positions, ranging from allowing all sins to prohibiting all sins absolutely. This lesson covers these positions in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on fatwa and actions
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the third area (fatwa) and then the five schools listed for the fourth area. Note the consensus on intentional error and the disagreement on forgetfulness.
The passage is dense with technical terms like الكبيرة and الصغيرة.
2
Identify the five schools and their positions
List each school and what it allows or forbids. Pay attention to the conditions like 'repulsiveness' or 'erroneous interpretation'.
The schools are: Hashwiyya, most Mu'tazila, al-Jubba'i, a fourth unnamed group, and Rafidites.
3
Compare the schools on scope of permissibility
Notice the progression from absolute permission to absolute prohibition. Consider how each school understands the nature of prophetic responsibility.
The fourth school uniquely allows forgetfulness but rebukes it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : ما يتعلق بالفتوى وأجمعت الأمة على أنه لا يجوز تعمد الخطأ، أما على سبيل السهو فقد اختلفوا فيه. الرابع : ما يتعلق بأفعالهم وأحوالهم وقد اختلفت فيه الأمة على خمسة مذاهب : الأول قول الحشوية وهو أنه يجوز عليهم الإقدام على الكبائر والصغائر. الثاني : أنه لا يجوز منهم تعمد الكبيرة ،البتة وأما تعمد الصغيرة فهو جائز بشرط أن لا يكون منفرًا، فأما إن كان تعمد الصغيرة منفرًا فذلك لا يجوز عليهم، مثل التطفيف بما دون الحبة وهذا قول أكثر المعتزلة. الثالث : أنه لا يجوز عليهم تعمد الكبيرة والصغيرة ولكن يجوز صدور الذنب منهم على سبيل الخطأ في التأويل، وهذا قول الجبائي. الرابع : أنه لا يجوز الكبيرة ولا الصغيرة لا تعمدًا ولا بالتأويل الخطأ، أما السهو والنسيان فجائزان عليهم، ثم إنهم يعاتبون على ذلك السهو والنسيان، لما أن علومهم أكمل، فكان الواجب عليهم المبالغة في الصدق والتحفظ والتيقظ. الخامس : أن لا يجوز عليهم الصغيرة ولا الكبيرة لا بالعمد ولا بالتأويل ولا بالسهو ولا بالنسيان وهذا مذهب الروافض واختلفت الأمة أيضًا في وقت وجوب هذه العصمة فالروافض قالت: إنها من أول الولادة إلى آخر العمر، وقال الأكثرون : هذه العصمة إنما تجب في زمان النبوة، وأما قبل النبوة فهي غير واجبة، وهو قول أكثر أصحابنا، وقول أبي الهذيل وأبي علي الجبائي.
Third: What pertains to fatwa. The community has agreed that intentional error is not permissible, but concerning forgetfulness, they have differed. Fourth: What pertains to their actions and states. The community has differed concerning it into five schools: First: The statement of the Hashwiyya—that committing major and minor sins is permissible for them. Second: That deliberate commission of a major sin is absolutely not permissible for them, but deliberate commission of a minor sin is permissible on condition that it does not cause repulsion; if deliberate commission of a minor sin is repulsive, then that is not permissible for them, like fraud in less than a grain—this is the view of most Mu'tazila. Third: That deliberate commission of a major or minor sin is not permissible for them, but the occurrence of sin from them by way of error in interpretation is permissible—this is the view of al-Jubba'i. Fourth: That major and minor sins are not permissible, neither deliberately nor through erroneous interpretation, but forgetfulness and oversight are permissible for them; then they are rebuked for that forgetfulness and oversight because their knowledge is more complete, so it was incumbent upon them to be extreme in truthfulness, caution, and vigilance. Fifth: That minor nor major sins are not permissible for them, neither deliberately nor through interpretation, nor by forgetfulness nor oversight—this is the school of the Rafidites. The community also differed concerning the time of the obligation of this infallibility: the Rafidites said it is from the beginning of birth to the end of life, and the majority said: this infallibility is only obligatory during the time of prophethood, but before prophethood it is not obligatory—this is the view of most of our companions, and the view of Abu al-Hudhayl and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the enumeration of the four areas, covering the third and fourth areas and then the timing of infallibility. The third area is fatwa (legal ruling): the community agrees a prophet cannot intentionally err in a fatwa, but differs on forgetfulness. The fourth area concerns actions and states, where Razi lists five schools: (1) Hashwiyya allow both major and minor sins; (2) most Mu'tazila forbid deliberate major sins but allow deliberate minor sins unless they are repulsive; (3) al-Jubba'i forbids deliberate major and minor sins but permits sins from erroneous interpretation; (4) another view forbids both intentionally and via interpretation but allows forgetfulness, with rebuke due to their higher knowledge; (5) the Rafidites absolutely forbid all sins in any way. Razi then adds that the community also differed on when infallibility applies: the Rafidites say from birth to death; the majority (including most Ash'aris, Abu al-Hudhayl, and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i) say it is only obligatory during prophethood.

الكبيرة
الصغيرة
الحشوية
المعتزلة
الجبائي
الرافضة

B) Sin via erroneous interpretation
C) Forgetfulness and oversight
D) All sins absolutely

Key Takeaway
The five schools on prophetic actions range from allowing all sins to prohibiting them entirely, with intermediate positions on minor sins, interpretation errors, and forgetfulness.

?
Which of the five schools do you find most convincing regarding prophetic fallibility in actions? How does that stance shape the way you look to the Prophet's example in your own moral decisions?
?
The fourth school rebukes prophets for forgetfulness because their knowledge is more complete. How does this heightened accountability challenge you in your own life—where might you be excusing your own negligence because 'I didn't know'?
?
If you believed, like the Rafidites, that prophets cannot have even forgetfulness, how would that affect your trust in their human experience? Conversely, if a prophet could sin through interpretation error, how would that impact your reliance on their rulings? Answer honestly: which view makes you feel more or less connected to the Prophet's humanity?

Timing of Infallibility: Before or During Prophethood?
Razi explains two views on the timing of infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major positions on whether prophetic infallibility applies before prophethood or only during it.

Core Idea
Infallibility is only required during prophethood, not before, according to the majority.

After discussing the areas of infallibility, Razi turns to a related question: when does this infallibility begin? Is a prophet protected from sin even before receiving revelation? The community differs, with the Rafidites arguing for lifelong infallibility and the majority (including most Ash'aris and some Mu'tazila) restricting it to the prophetic period. This lesson examines these two views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on timing
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It presents two views on the timing of infallibility.
Pay attention to the terms 'قبل النبوة' (before prophethood) and 'زمان النبوة' (time of prophethood).
2
Identify the two opposing views
List the Rafidite view (from birth to death) and the majority view (only during prophethood). Note who is included in the majority.
The majority includes 'most of our companions' (Ash'aris) and Abu al-Hudhayl and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the majority might restrict infallibility to prophethood. The passage does not give reasons, but it implies that before prophethood, the prophet is not divinely protected from sin.
This does not mean prophets sinned before prophethood, only that it was not obligatory for them to be infallible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : ما يتعلق بالفتوى وأجمعت الأمة على أنه لا يجوز تعمد الخطأ، أما على سبيل السهو فقد اختلفوا فيه. الرابع : ما يتعلق بأفعالهم وأحوالهم وقد اختلفت فيه الأمة على خمسة مذاهب : الأول قول الحشوية وهو أنه يجوز عليهم الإقدام على الكبائر والصغائر. الثاني : أنه لا يجوز منهم تعمد الكبيرة ،البتة وأما تعمد الصغيرة فهو جائز بشرط أن لا يكون منفرًا، فأما إن كان تعمد الصغيرة منفرًا فذلك لا يجوز عليهم، مثل التطفيف بما دون الحبة وهذا قول أكثر المعتزلة. الثالث : أنه لا يجوز عليهم تعمد الكبيرة والصغيرة ولكن يجوز صدور الذنب منهم على سبيل الخطأ في التأويل، وهذا قول الجبائي. الرابع : أنه لا يجوز الكبيرة ولا الصغيرة لا تعمدًا ولا بالتأويل الخطأ، أما السهو والنسيان فجائزان عليهم، ثم إنهم يعاتبون على ذلك السهو والنسيان، لما أن علومهم أكمل، فكان الواجب عليهم المبالغة في الصدق والتحفظ والتيقظ. الخامس : أن لا يجوز عليهم الصغيرة ولا الكبيرة لا بالعمد ولا بالتأويل ولا بالسهو ولا بالنسيان وهذا مذهب الروافض واختلفت الأمة أيضًا في وقت وجوب هذه العصمة فالروافض قالت: إنها من أول الولادة إلى آخر العمر، وقال الأكثرون : هذه العصمة إنما تجب في زمان النبوة، وأما قبل النبوة فهي غير واجبة، وهو قول أكثر أصحابنا، وقول أبي الهذيل وأبي علي الجبائي.
Third: What pertains to fatwa. The community has agreed that intentional error is not permissible, but concerning forgetfulness, they have differed. Fourth: What pertains to their actions and states. The community has differed concerning it into five schools: First: The statement of the Hashwiyya—that committing major and minor sins is permissible for them. Second: That deliberate commission of a major sin is absolutely not permissible for them, but deliberate commission of a minor sin is permissible on condition that it does not cause repulsion; if deliberate commission of a minor sin is repulsive, then that is not permissible for them, like fraud in less than a grain—this is the view of most Mu'tazila. Third: That deliberate commission of a major or minor sin is not permissible for them, but the occurrence of sin from them by way of error in interpretation is permissible—this is the view of al-Jubba'i. Fourth: That major and minor sins are not permissible, neither deliberately nor through erroneous interpretation, but forgetfulness and oversight are permissible for them; then they are rebuked for that forgetfulness and oversight because their knowledge is more complete, so it was incumbent upon them to be extreme in truthfulness, caution, and vigilance. Fifth: That minor nor major sins are not permissible for them, neither deliberately nor through interpretation, nor by forgetfulness nor oversight—this is the school of the Rafidites. The community also differed concerning the time of the obligation of this infallibility: the Rafidites said it is from the beginning of birth to the end of life, and the majority said: this infallibility is only obligatory during the time of prophethood, but before prophethood it is not obligatory—this is the view of most of our companions, and the view of Abu al-Hudhayl and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the enumeration of the four areas, covering the third and fourth areas and then the timing of infallibility. The third area is fatwa (legal ruling): the community agrees a prophet cannot intentionally err in a fatwa, but differs on forgetfulness. The fourth area concerns actions and states, where Razi lists five schools: (1) Hashwiyya allow both major and minor sins; (2) most Mu'tazila forbid deliberate major sins but allow deliberate minor sins unless they are repulsive; (3) al-Jubba'i forbids deliberate major and minor sins but permits sins from erroneous interpretation; (4) another view forbids both intentionally and via interpretation but allows forgetfulness, with rebuke due to their higher knowledge; (5) the Rafidites absolutely forbid all sins in any way. Razi then adds that the community also differed on when infallibility applies: the Rafidites say from birth to death; the majority (including most Ash'aris, Abu al-Hudhayl, and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i) say it is only obligatory during prophethood.

Key Terms
عصمة
وقت وجوب
الروافض
قبل النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that prophets are infallible from birth.
Correction: The majority holds that infallibility is only required during prophethood, not before.

Checkpoint

A) From birth to death
B) Only during prophethood
C) Only after prophethood
D) At all times

Key Takeaway
The majority of theologians hold that prophets are infallible only during their prophetic mission, not before.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Razi states that infallibility is only 'obligatory' during prophethood. If God does not require sinlessness from you before He calls you to a task, what excuse do you have for not stepping up to serve Him because of your past mistakes? What step will you take this week to act despite your imperfections?

Razi's View on Prophetic Infallibility
Razi's definition of prophetic infallibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's specific position that prophets are infallible from intentional major and minor sins, but forgetfulness is permissible.

Core Idea
Infallibility covers intentional sins only; forgetfulness is not a sin.

Imam Razi opens this section by clearly stating his own view on prophetic infallibility. He distinguishes between intentional sins and those committed by forgetfulness. This distinction is crucial because it sets the scope of infallibility. Let's read his statement carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic statement
Read Razi's statement in Arabic to appreciate its precision. Note the key terms 'الكبائر' (major sins) and 'الصغائر' (minor sins).
Razi uses the phrase 'في زمان النبوة' (during the time of prophethood) to limit the scope.
2
Understand the distinction
Razi says prophets are infallible from intentional sins ('بالعمد') but not from forgetfulness ('على سبيل السهو'). Focus on why forgetfulness is treated differently.
Forgetfulness is not a deliberate act, so it does not contradict the purpose of prophethood.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider the difference between this view and other scholarly opinions. Razi's view is moderate, avoiding extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي نقوله : إن الأنبياء - صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم - معصومون في زمان النبوة من الكبائر والصغائر بالعمد أما على سبيل السهو فجائز، ويدل على وجوب العصمة وجوه : الحجة الأولى : لو صدر الذنب عنهم لكان حالهم في استحقاق الذم عاجلا والعقاب آجلا أشد من حال عصاة الأمة، وهذا باطل، فصدور الذنب عنهم أيضا باطل بيان الملازمة أن أعظم نعم الله على العباد عطاؤهم نعمة الرسالة والنبوة، وكل من كانت نعم الله تعالى عليه أكثر كان صدور الذنب عنه أفحش، وصريح العقل يدل عليه، ثم يؤكده من النقل وجوه. أحدها : قوله : ينسَاءَ النَّبِيِّ لَسْتُنَّ كَأَحَدٍ مِّنَ النِّسَاء إِنِ اتَّقَيْتُ) [الأحزاب: ٣٢]، هو مَن يَأْتِ مِنكُنَ بِفَاحِشَةٍ مُّبَيِّنَةٍ يُضَعَفْ لَهَا الْعَذَابُ ضِعْفَيْنِ وكان ذالك على الله يسير المكان [الأحزاب: ٣٠] وثانيها : أن المحصن يرجم، وغيره يجلد. والثالث : أن العبد يحد نصف حد الحر. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو صدر الذنب منهم لكان حالهم في استحقاق الذم العاجل والعقاب الآجل فوق حال عصاة الأمة، إلا أن هذا باطل بالإجماع؛ فإن أحدًا لا يجوز أن يقول : الرسول أخس حالا عند الله تعالى وأقل مرتبة من كل واحد من اللصوص والزناة، وهذا يدل على عدم صدور الذنب عنهم.
And what we say: The prophets—may God's blessings and peace be upon them—are infallible during the time of prophethood from major and minor sins intentionally; as for by forgetfulness, it is permissible. That which indicates the obligation of infallibility are several proofs. The first proof: If sin were to occur from them, their state in deserving blame immediately and punishment later would be more severe than the state of the sinners of the community, and this is false. Therefore, the occurrence of sin from them is also false. The explanation of the entailment: The greatest of God's blessings upon servants is His bestowing upon them the grace of messengership and prophethood. And whoever has more blessings from God Almighty upon him, the occurrence of sin from him is more heinous. Pure reason indicates this. Then it is confirmed from transmitted evidence by several aspects. One of them: His saying, 'O wives of the Prophet, you are not like any other women, if you are righteous' [33:32]; and 'Whoever of you commits a manifest indecency, the punishment will be doubled for her, and that is easy for God' [33:30]. The second: that the married person is stoned, while others are flogged. The third: that the slave is given half the punishment of a free person. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if sin were to occur from them, their state in deserving immediate blame and future punishment would be above the state of the sinners of the community, except that this is false by consensus; for no one may say: the Messenger is in a worse state before God Almighty and lower in rank than every single thief and fornicator. This indicates the non-occurrence of sin from them.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's own position and his first proof. Razi states that prophets are infallible during the period of prophethood from major and minor sins when committed intentionally, but forgetfulness is permissible. He then provides the first proof, which is a rational argument: if a prophet committed a sin, he would deserve more blame and punishment than ordinary sinners because he has received the greatest blessings (prophethood). This is heinous in reason, and it is confirmed by scriptural evidence: the wives of the Prophet are addressed with a double punishment for sin (Surah al-Ahzab), the married person (muhsan) gets a harsher punishment (stoning) than the unmarried (flogging), and the slave gets half the punishment of a free person. All these show that greater grace implies greater punishment for sin. Therefore, if prophets sinned, they would be more blameworthy than common sinners. But it is consensually false to say the Prophet is worse than thieves and fornicators. Hence, prophets cannot sin.

Key Terms
عصمة
الكبيرة
الصغيرة
الذنب
النبوة
الرسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are completely infallible in all actions, including unintentional ones.
Correction: Razi teaches that infallibility applies to intentional sins; forgetfulness is permissible, so unintentional lapses do not violate infallibility.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, prophets are infallible from which types of sins?
A) Only major sins
B) Only minor sins
C) Both major and minor sins intentionally
D) All sins including forgetfulness

Key Takeaway
Razi defines prophetic infallibility as protection from intentional major and minor sins, while forgetfulness is not a violation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you often excuse yourself by saying 'I forgot' or 'I didn't mean it'? In light of Razi's teaching that forgetfulness is permissible for prophets but intentional sin is not, how honestly do you assess the intention behind your own actions? Will you commit today to examining the real motive of your heart before making excuses?
?
If the prophets themselves were only guaranteed protection from intentional sins, how much more careful must you be about your own deliberate choices? What intentional sin are you currently tolerating that you know is wrong? What step will you take this week to abandon it, seeking God's help?
?
Razi's distinction shows that God's protection is about the heart's intent, not external perfection. Have you been relying on external rituals while neglecting the inner state of your soul? Where in your life is your intention mixed with hypocrisy or self-interest? What concrete change will you make today to purify your intention for Allah alone?

The First Proof: Greater Blessings Intensify Sin
Razi's first proof using rational and scriptural arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural argument that prophets cannot sin because their greater blessings make sin more heinous.

Core Idea
More divine grace means a sin is more severe, so prophets must be sinless.

Razi now presents his first proof for the necessity of prophetic infallibility. He argues from a rational principle: the more God has blessed someone, the more egregious their sin would be. Since prophets receive the greatest blessing—prophethood—any sin from them would be unimaginably heinous. He then supports this with three scriptural analogies. Let's examine this proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the rational premise
Razi states that the one who receives greater blessings commits a more heinous sin. Understand why this is rationally necessary.
This is a principle of common sense: the more you owe, the worse the betrayal.
2
Examine the scriptural analogies
Razi gives three examples: the wives of the Prophet receive double punishment, the married person is stoned, and a slave gets half the punishment. Each shows that greater privilege means greater accountability.
The first analogy is directly from the Quran.
3
Apply to prophets
If prophets sinned, they would deserve more blame than the worst sinners. But that is unacceptable by consensus. Therefore, they cannot sin.
The conclusion is reached by contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Second Proof: Prophetic Infallibility from Testimony
Razi provides a second proof: if prophets sinned, their testimony would be rejected according to Quranic ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second proof for prophetic infallibility, which uses the Quranic ruling on accepting testimony from a fasiq to argue that prophets must be sinless.

Core Idea
A prophet's testimony must be accepted; a sinner's testimony is suspect.

Imam Razi continues his defense of prophetic infallibility with a second proof drawn from the Quran. He argues that if prophets could sin, they would be classified as fasiq, and the Quran commands us to verify news from such a person. This would undermine the very purpose of prophethood. Read the passage carefully, noting how Razi grounds his argument in a specific verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice that the passage is incomplete; it cuts off before the conclusion. Focus on the premise that is presented.
The source text ends with 'إلا أن' (except that...), indicating the conclusion is missing.
2
Identify the proof structure
Razi states a conditional: if sin occurred from prophets, their testimony would not be accepted. He then cites Quran 49:6 as evidence. Ask yourself: how does the verse support the conditional?
3
Connect the concept of fasiq to prophets
The verse commands caution when a fasiq brings news. If prophets could sin, they would be fasiq, and their prophetic testimony would require verification—contradicting their role as trustworthy messengers.
This is the missing logical conclusion implied by the premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو صدر عنهم الذنب لما كانوا مقبولي الشهادة ؛ لقوله تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِن جَاءَكُمْ فَاسِقٌ بِنَبَاءٍ فَتَبَيَّنُوا أَن تُصِيبُوا قَوْمًا بِجَهَالَةٍ فَتُصْبِحُوا عَلَى مَا فَعَلْتُمْ نَادِمِينَ [الحجرات: ٦] أمرنا بالتثبت والتوقف في قبول شهادة الفاسق، إلا أن
The second proof: If sin were to occur from them, they would not be acceptable in testimony; because of His saying, 'O you who have believed, if a fasiq (sinner) comes to you with news, then verify it, lest you harm people out of ignorance and become regretful over what you have done' [49:6]. He commanded us to be cautious and to pause in accepting the testimony of the fasiq, except that...
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage introduces the second proof for prophetic infallibility. Razi argues that if a prophet committed a sin, he would be considered a fasiq (sinner). The Quran (49:6) commands believers to verify news brought by a fasiq and not to accept his testimony without caution. Since prophets are bearers of divine testimony (revelation), they must be free from sin to ensure their testimony is accepted. The text cuts off before completing the argument, but the implication is that prophets cannot sin because otherwise their testimony (prophethood) would be rejected.

الشهادة
فاسق

Checkpoint
What does Razi argue would happen if a prophet committed a sin?
A) The prophet would be forgiven immediately
B) The prophet would no longer be a prophet
C) The prophet's testimony would not be accepted due to being a fasiq
D) The prophet would be punished by stoning

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the Quranic ruling on fasiq testimony to argue that prophets must be sinless, as their testimony (revelation) must be accepted without verification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the Prophet was sinless and his testimony is fully accepted, why do you still hesitate to follow some of his commands? Which command do you find hardest to accept, and how does this proof of infallibility confront your reluctance?
?
The Quran teaches us to pause and verify news from a fasiq. Think about the last time you spread something without verifying. How does this verse hold you accountable, and what step will you take today to change this habit?
?
Are you 'maqbul al-shahadah' — acceptable in testimony by your character? If your testimony were questioned like a fasiq's, would your words carry weight? What does this lesson teach you about the importance of integrity in your own speech and witness?

Scope of Prophetic Infallibility: Forgetfulness and Sin
Imam Razi discusses permissibility of forgetfulness and Rawafid absolute infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets can experience forgetfulness and are blamed for it, and that the Rawafid (Shia) believe they are infallible from all sins including forgetfulness.

Core Idea
Prophets are not infallible from forgetfulness, but they are blameworthy for it.

Imam Razi begins by addressing the scope of prophetic infallibility. He explains that forgetfulness is permissible for prophets, yet they are still held accountable due to their higher knowledge. He then presents an extreme view that prohibits any sin, even unintentional, which is attributed to the Rawafid. This lesson unpacks these positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation to grasp the two main points: the permissibility of forgetfulness and the Rawafid doctrine.
Pay attention to the blame aspect – it contrasts with absolute infallibility.
2
Understand the blame for forgetfulness
Notice that even though forgetfulness is allowed, prophets are blamed because their knowledge is more complete. This shows a nuanced view of infallibility.
The blame is not punishment but a mark of higher responsibility.
3
Identify the Rawafid position
The Rawafid hold that no sin, small or great, is permissible for prophets under any circumstance. This is the most absolute view mentioned.
Contrast this with the earlier statement that forgetfulness is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السهو والنسيان فجائزان عليهم، ثم إنهم يعاتبون على ذلك السهو والنسيان، لما أن علومهم أكمل، فكان الواجب عليهم المبالغة في الصدق والتحفظ والتيقظ. الخامس : أن لا يجوز عليهم الصغيرة ولا الكبيرة لا بالعمد ولا بالتأويل ولا بالسهو ولا بالنسيان وهذا مذهب الروافض. واختلفت الأمة أيضًا في وقت وجوب هذه العصمة فالروافض قالت: إنها من أول الولادة إلى آخر العمر، وقال الأكثرون : هذه العصمة إنما تجب في زمان النبوة، وأما قبل النبوة فهي غير واجبة، وهو قول أكثر أصحابنا، وقول أبي الهذيل وأبي علي الجبائي. والذي نقوله : إن الأنبياء - صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم - معصومون في زمان النبوة من الكبائر والصغائر بالعمد أما على سبيل السهو فجائز، ويدل على وجوب العصمة وجوه :
Forgetfulness and oversight are permissible for them, then they are blamed for that forgetfulness and oversight, because their knowledge is more complete, so it was incumbent upon them to be extreme in truthfulness, caution, and vigilance. The fifth: that [sins] small and great are not permissible for them, neither intentionally nor through interpretation nor through forgetfulness nor through oversight, and this is the doctrine of the Rawafid. The community also differed concerning the time when this infallibility is obligatory. The Rawafid said: it is from the beginning of birth until the end of life. The majority said: this infallibility is only obligatory during the time of prophethood, but before prophethood it is not obligatory, and this is the saying of most of our companions, and the saying of Abu Hudhayl and Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i. And what we say: the prophets – peace and blessings of God be upon them – are infallible during the time of prophethood from major and minor sins intentionally, but as for forgetfulness, it is permissible. And that which indicates the obligation of infallibility are proofs:
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the author's position on prophetic infallibility after reviewing differing opinions. It begins by noting that forgetfulness and oversight are permissible for prophets, yet they are blamed for them because of their complete knowledge. Then he lists the fifth opinion: the Rawafid (Shia) hold that no sin, small or great, is permissible for prophets in any circumstance. Next, he mentions disagreement on the timing of infallibility: the Rawafid say from birth to death, while the majority (including most of the author's school, Abu Hudhayl, and Abu Ali al-Jubba'i) say it is only during the period of prophethood. Finally, the author states his own view: prophets are infallible from major and minor intentional sins during prophethood, but forgetfulness is possible. He then announces that proofs will follow.

Key Terms
سهو
نسيان
عصمة
روافض
صغيرة
كبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are infallible in every action, including forgetfulness.
Correction: Imam Razi explicitly says forgetfulness is permissible, though prophets are blamed for it.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, why are prophets blamed for forgetfulness?
A) Because forgetfulness is a sin
B) Because their knowledge is more complete
C) Because they are not infallible
D) Because the Rawafid said so

Key Takeaway
Prophets can forget but are held to a higher standard because of their complete knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that prophets, despite their complete knowledge, are blamed for forgetfulness. You have less knowledge and more excuses. Does your conscience hold you accountable for your lapses, or do you rationalize them away? Will you commit to a specific change in how you approach your responsibilities?
?
The passage says prophets are expected to be 'extreme in truthfulness, caution, and vigilance.' Compare that to your own standard. In what area of your life are you most careless with the truth? What is one step you can take today to increase your vigilance?

Timing of Prophetic Infallibility: Before and During Prophethood
Imam Razi compares timing views and states his own position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement on when infallibility begins: from birth (Rawafid) vs only during prophethood (majority), and Imam Razi's own view that infallibility applies during prophethood but forgetfulness is permissible.

Core Idea
Infallibility is required only during the prophetic mission, not before.

After discussing the scope, Imam Razi turns to the timing of infallibility. He reports the Rawafid claim that prophets are infallible from birth, while the majority holds that infallibility begins with prophethood. He then states his own position, aligning with the majority but allowing forgetfulness during prophethood. This lesson focuses on these key differences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the two contrasting views on timing and the author's final position.
The phrase 'واختلفت الأمة أيضًا' signals a new topic.
2
Distinguish the timing views
Identify the Rawafid view (from birth to death) and the majority view (only during prophethood). Note who the majority includes.
The majority includes most of Imam Razi's school and two named scholars.
3
Understand Imam Razi's position
He states that prophets are infallible from major and minor intentional sins during prophethood, but forgetfulness is still permissible.
This combines the majority timing view with the earlier scope view.

First Proof: Greater Blessings Make Sin Worse
Imam Razi presents the first proof for prophetic infallibility using an a fortiori argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the a fortiori argument for prophetic infallibility based on the correlation between blessings and sin severity.

Core Idea
The greater the blessing, the more heinous the sin — so prophets cannot sin.

Imam Razi begins by asserting that if prophets sinned, they would be more blameworthy than any other sinner because they have received the greatest blessings. This seems impossible by consensus, so the premise must be false. Let's walk through the proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a compressed logical style.
2
Identify the main premise
The proof hinges on the correlation: the greater the blessings, the more heinous the sin. Find where Razi states this and how he supports it with reason.
This is the core of the a fortiori argument.
3
Examine the scriptural supports
Razi gives three examples from revelation that reinforce the premise. Read them and see how they illustrate the same principle.
The wives of the Prophet, married adulterers, and slaves show gradation of punishment.
4
Understand the conclusion
The argument concludes that if prophets sinned, they would be worse than all sinners, which is impossible by consensus. Therefore, prophets do not sin.
This shows the power of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : لو صدر الذنب عنهم لكان حالهم في استحقاق الذم عاجلا والعقاب آجلا أشد من حال عصاة الأمة، وهذا باطل، فصدور الذنب عنهم أيضا باطل بيان الملازمة أن أعظم نعم الله على العباد عطاؤهم نعمة الرسالة والنبوة، وكل من كانت نعم الله تعالى عليه أكثر كان صدور الذنب عنه أفحش، وصريح العقل يدل عليه، ثم يؤكده من النقل وجوه. أحدها : قوله : يَا نِسَاءَ النَّبِيِّ لَسْتُنَّ كَأَحَدٍ مِّنَ النِّسَاءِ إِنِ اتَّقَيْتُنَّ [الأحزاب: ٣٢]، فَمَن يَأْتِ مِنكُنَّ بِفَاحِشَةٍ مُّبَيِّنَةٍ يُضَاعَفْ لَهَا الْعَذَابُ ضِعْفَيْنِ وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ عَلَى اللَّهِ يَسِيرًا [الأحزاب: ٣٠] وثانيها : أن المحصن يرجم، وغيره يجلد. والثالث : أن العبد يحد نصف حد الحر. فثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو صدر الذنب منهم لكان حالهم في استحقاق الذم العاجل والعقاب الآجل فوق حال جميع عصاة الأمة، إلا أن هذا باطل بالإجماع؛ فإن أحدًا لا يجوز أن يقول : الرسول أخس حالا عند الله تعالى وأقل مرتبة من كل واحد من اللصوص والزناة، وهذا يدل على عدم صدور الذنب عنهم.
The first proof: If sin occurred from them, then their state in deserving immediate blame and ultimate punishment would be more severe than the state of the sinful of the community, and this is false, so the occurrence of sin from them is also false. The explanation of the correlation: the greatest of God's blessings upon servants is His granting them the blessing of messengership and prophethood, and whoever has more of God's blessings upon him, the occurrence of sin from him is more heinous, and pure reason indicates it. Then it is supported from transmitted evidence in ways: One of them: His saying: 'O wives of the Prophet, you are not like any other women if you are righteous, so if any of you commits a clear lewdness, the punishment will be doubled for her, and that is easy for Allah' [Al-Ahzab:32,30]. The second: that the married adulterer is stoned, while others are flogged. The third: that the slave is flogged half the punishment of a free man. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if sin occurred from them, their state in deserving immediate blame and ultimate punishment would be above the state of all the sinful of the community, but this is false by consensus; for no one may say that the messenger is in a worse state before God and of a lower rank than every thief and adulterer. And this indicates that sin does not occur from them.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for prophetic infallibility. It is an argument a fortiori. The proof proceeds as follows: if prophets committed sins, they would deserve more blame and punishment than ordinary Muslims because they have received the greatest blessings (prophethood). Reason dictates that the more blessed a person is, the more heinous his sin. This is supported by scriptural examples: the wives of the Prophet are warned of doubled punishment; married adulterers receive a harsher punishment than unmarried ones; slaves receive half the punishment of free persons. The conclusion is that if a prophet sinned, he would be worse than any sinful person, which is impossible by consensus. Therefore, prophets do not commit sins.

Key Terms
ذنب
استحقاق الذم
العقاب الآجل
أفحش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets could sin and then repent, making their sin forgivable.
Correction: This proof shows that if they sinned, they would be more blameworthy than any other sinner, which is impossible. Therefore, the very occurrence of sin from them is impossible, not just repented.

Checkpoint
What is the rationale behind the first proof?
A) Prophets are too busy to sin
B) Prophets receive greater blessings, so their sins would be worse
C) God forgives prophets always
D) Sins are impossible for any human

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot sin because their greater blessings would make their sin worse than any other's, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If greater blessings make sin more heinous, how do you view the sins you commit despite the countless blessings God has given you? Are you not more blameworthy than someone who has received less? What would it mean for you to treat your own sins with the seriousness they deserve, knowing this principle?
?
This lesson argues that prophets cannot sin because their status makes their sin worse than any other. But as a believer who claims to follow the Prophet, do you ever act as if his example is optional? In what area of your life have you ignored his guidance, and how does that compare to the gravity the lesson describes?
?
Consensus says no one can claim a prophet is lower than a thief or adulterer. Yet, in your heart, do you ever secretly think that some sins are 'small' because they are common? How does this proof challenge your own scale of what is 'bad' and call you to re-evaluate your attitude toward disobedience?

Second Proof: Prophets as Accepted Witnesses
Imam Razi argues from legal disqualification of sinners to prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophetic infallibility is necessary based on the requirement that a witness's testimony be accepted and the high status of prophets as witnesses for all mankind.

Core Idea
A sinner's testimony is rejected; prophets are accepted witnesses for all religion.

Imam Razi presents a powerful legal argument: if prophets could sin, they would be considered sinful (fasiq), and the Quran commands us to reject the testimony of a fasiq. But this contradicts their role as witnesses for the entire religion and as the ultimate witness on the Day of Judgment. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: first a conditional statement, then a Quranic proof, then a climax showing the absurdity of rejecting prophetic testimony.
2
Understand the legal principle
The Quran (49:6) commands verification of news from a fasiq. This implies a fasiq's testimony is not accepted. Grasp this foundational point.
In Islamic law, a fasiq's testimony is rejected in legal matters.
3
Apply to prophets
If prophets sinned, they would be fasiq. Then their testimony would be rejected. But this is absurd—prophets are witnesses for the entire religion and for all mankind.
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verses
The passage cites two verses: one about rejecting the fasiq's news, and another affirming that the Prophet is a witness over all. Contemplate how the second verse reinforces the first argument.
Verse 2:143 establishes the Prophet's role as witness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو صدر عنهم الذنب لما كانوا مقبولي الشهادة ؛ لقوله تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِن جَاءَكُمْ فَاسِقٌ بِنَبَأٍ فَتَبَيَّنُوا أَن تُصِيبُوا قَوْمًا بِجَهَالَةٍ فَتُصْبِحُوا عَلَى مَا فَعَلْتُمْ نَادِمِينَ [الحجرات: ٦] أمرنا بالتثبت والتوقف في قبول شهادة الفاسق، إلا أن هذا باطل، فإن من لم تقبل شهادته في الحبة كيف تقبل شهادته في الأديان الثابتة إلى يوم القيامة ؟! وأيضًا : فإن الله تعالى شهد بأن محمدًا شهيد على الكل يوم القيامة، قال الله تعالى : لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَيَكُونَ الرَّسُولُ عَلَيْكُمْ شَهِيدًا [البقرة: ١٤٣] ومن كان شهيدًا لجميع الرسل يوم القيامة كيف يكون بحال لا تقبل شهادته في الحبة ؟!
The second proof: If sin occurred from them, they would not be accepted in testimony; because of His saying: 'O you who believe, if a wicked person comes to you with news, then verify [it] lest you harm a people out of ignorance and become regretful over what you did' [Al-Hujurat:6]. He commanded us to be cautious and to pause in accepting the testimony of a wicked person. But this is false, for if his testimony in a small matter is not accepted, how can his testimony be accepted concerning the established religions until the Day of Judgment?! Also, God testified that Muhammad is a witness over all on the Day of Resurrection. God said: 'So that you may be witnesses over mankind and the Messenger may be a witness over you' [Al-Baqarah:143]. And how can one who is a witness for all the messengers on the Day of Resurrection be in a state where his testimony in a small matter is not accepted?!
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for prophetic infallibility. It argues that if prophets committed sins, they would be considered sinful (fasiq) and their testimony would be rejected, as per the Quranic command to verify the news of a fasiq. But this would be absurd because prophets are witnesses for the entire religion and for all mankind on the Day of Judgment. If their testimony on a small worldly matter were rejected, how could they be accepted as witnesses for the entire religion? Moreover, God himself testifies that Muhammad is a witness over all, implying his testimony is accepted. Thus, prophets cannot be sinful.

Key Terms
شهادة
فاسق
شهيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could sin and then repent, but that does not affect their testimony.
Correction: The argument is not about repentance but about the legal status of a fasiq: a fasiq's testimony is rejected even after repentance until he is proven trustworthy again. Moreover, the proof focuses on the contradiction between being a fasiq and being a witness for all religion.

Checkpoint
Why does the second proof consider it impossible for prophets to sin?
A) Sinners cannot be prophets
B) God would not choose a sinner
C) Sinners' testimony is rejected, but prophets are witnesses for all religion
D) Prophets are immune to temptation

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot sin because their testimony as witnesses for the entire religion would be invalidated if they were sinners—a contradiction that proves their infallibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that even a small sin would disqualify a prophet from being a reliable witness. Consider your own life: are there 'small sins' you tolerate that undermine your credibility when you speak about Islam to others? How will you address them today?
?
If the Prophet's testimony is accepted because of his sinlessness, how seriously do you take your own responsibility to be a truthful witness? In what specific situation this week have you, by your words or actions, misrepresented Islam? What will you change?
?
The proof uses an absurdity: a prophet's testimony rejected in a small matter but accepted in the greatest. Reflect: are there contradictions in your own faith where you claim to trust Allah's revelation for the big questions but disobey in 'small' matters? What would it take for you to live consistently?

Third Proof: Sin Impossible Due to Rebuke Prohibition
Razi's third proof using commanding good and forbidding evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's third proof that prophets cannot sin, based on the obligation to rebuke sinners and the prohibition of rebuking prophets.

Core Idea
If prophets sinned, rebuke would be required—but rebuking a prophet is forbidden, so sin is impossible.

Imam Razi presents a tightly argued proof using a universal principle of Islamic ethics: the obligation to command good and forbid evil. He reasons that if a prophet sinned, rebuke would be obligatory. Yet rebuking a prophet is itself a grave sin, as harming God's messenger is cursed. Thus, sin must be impossible for prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the concise logical structure: if sin, then rebuke; but rebuke forbidden; therefore sin impossible.
The verse from Al-Ahzab is key.
2
Identify the premises
The proof has two main premises: (1) sin makes rebuke obligatory, and (2) rebuking prophets is forbidden. Find them in the text.
3
Understand the conclusion
Combine the premises: if sin occurred, rebuke would be needed, but rebuke is not allowed, so the original sin cannot occur.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this proof does not rely on the prophet's perfection but on the logical impossibility of a required but forbidden act.
This is a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو صدر الذنب عنهم لوجب زجرهم ؛ لأن الدلائل الدالة على وجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر عامة، لكن زجر الأنبياء غير جائز، لقول الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُؤْذُونَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ لَعَنَهُمُ اللهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَة﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٧] فكان صدور الذنب عنهم ممتنعا.
The third proof: If sin occurred from them, it would be necessary to rebuke them; because the evidences indicating the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil are general, but rebuking the prophets is not permissible, because of God's saying: 'Indeed, those who harm God and His Messenger, God has cursed them in this world and the Hereafter' [Al-Ahzab:57]. So the occurrence of sin from them is prevented.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This third proof is based on the principle of commanding good and forbidding evil. If prophets committed sins, it would be obligatory to rebuke them (as part of forbidding evil). However, rebuking a prophet is itself forbidden, as harming the Prophet is cursed by God. Therefore, prophets cannot sin, because if they did, they would necessitate an act (rebuke) that is prohibited. Thus, sin from them is impossible.

Key Terms
زجر
الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر
إيذاء الله ورسوله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof relies on the inherent perfection of the prophet.
Correction: The proof relies on the logical impossibility of a required act (rebuke) being forbidden, not on the prophet's attributes.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of a prophet sinning according to the third proof?
A) He would be punished
B) He would be rebuked
C) He would lose prophethood
D) He would be forgiven automatically

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot sin because if they did, they would need to be rebuked, but rebuking a prophet is itself a sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If rebuking a prophet is a sin, how does that affect your attitude when you hear about the Prophet's life? Do you ever find yourself criticizing or questioning his actions? Reflect on your heart's posture toward the Prophet. What will you do to ensure you never harm him even in your thoughts?
?
The proof shows that rebuking a prophet is forbidden because it harms them. Think about your own words and actions. Do you ever speak ill of the scholars or pious people? How does this principle extend to them? Commit to one change in your speech today.
?
If sin is impossible for prophets, what does that mean for your trust in their message? Can you fully submit to their teachings without doubt? Ask yourself: Do I truly believe that the Prophet never erred in conveying the message? If not, what is holding you back from that conviction?

Fourth Proof: The Dilemma of Prophetic Sinlessness
Imam Razi's fourth proof: a dilemma on prophetic sinlessness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a prophet's sinlessness is necessary for the consistency of divine command.

Core Idea
A prophet's sin would force God to contradict Himself.

Imam al-Razi presents a logical argument known as a dilemma to prove that a prophet cannot commit sin. The argument shows that if the prophet were to sin, it would lead to an impossible situation regarding divine commands. This passage from his work *Al-Arba‘in* demonstrates the rational necessity of prophetic sinlessness.

Guided Path
1
Read the original passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own reasoning come through.
Notice the structure: a conditional statement leading to two alternatives.
2
Analyse the dilemma structure
Identify the two horns of the dilemma: either we are commanded to follow the sinful prophet, or we are not. Understand why each option is impossible.
3
Connect to the Qur'anic evidence
See how Imam Razi uses the Qur'anic verse (Al-Imran 3:31) to refute the second option. The verse commands following the prophet unconditionally.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Since both options are false, the initial premise (that the prophet could sin) must be false. This establishes sinlessness as a rational necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : لو صدر الفسق عن محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم لكنا إما أن نكون مأمورين بالاقتداء به، وذلك باطل لأن الأمر بالفسق لا يجوز على الحكيم، أو لا نكون مأمورين بالاقتداء به، وهو باطل، لقوله تعالى : قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ الله [آل عمران: ٣١] ولما كان صدور الفسق عنه يفضي إلى أحد هذين القسمين الباطلين كان صدور الفسق عنه محالا.
The fourth proof: If wickedness occurred from Muhammad (peace be upon him), then either we would be commanded to follow him – and this is false because commanding wickedness is not permissible from the Wise – or we would not be commanded to follow him, which is false because of His saying: 'Say, if you love God, follow me, and God will love you' [Al-Imran:31]. And since the occurrence of wickedness from him would lead to one of these two false possibilities, the occurrence of wickedness from him is impossible.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This fourth proof is a dilemma. If the Prophet committed a sin, then either we are commanded to follow him in that sin or we are not. If we are commanded to follow him, then God would be commanding sin, which is impossible for a Wise God. If we are not commanded to follow him, then the Quranic command to follow the Prophet would be violated. Both options are false, so the Prophet cannot sin.

Key Terms
الاقتداء
الفسق
الحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof shows that the Prophet cannot err in matters of judgment or worldly affairs.
Correction: The proof specifically targets intentional sin (فسق) and shows that a sinful action by the Prophet would put the divine command in contradiction. It does not address errors in ijtihad or forgetfulness.

Checkpoint
What is the dilemma presented in the fourth proof?
A) Either the Prophet is sinless or he is not
B) Either we follow him in sin or we do not, both impossible
C) Either God punishes him or forgives him
D) Either he is a prophet or he is not

Key Takeaway
The prophet's sinlessness is rationally necessary to avoid contradiction in divine commands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that following the Prophet is a direct command from God. In your daily life, where do you realize you are not fully following the Prophet, even in small matters? What would it cost you to align that area with his example?
?
The dilemma assumes that any sin by the Prophet would make God a commander of evil. Do you hold the Prophet's sinlessness as a mere belief, or does it actively shape how you trust his guidance without question? Where do you struggle to submit to his teachings because they contradict your desires?
?
God's wisdom prohibits commanding sin. When you find yourself rationalizing a sin, are you effectively attributing weakness to God's command? How can you train your heart to see every command as wise and beneficial, even when it is hard?

Fifth Proof: Sin Would Entail Threat of Hell and Curse
Imam Razi's fifth proof for prophetic sinlessness using Quranic threats.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the threat of Hell and curse logically necessitates the sinlessness of prophets.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot be under threat of Hell or curse, so they must be sinless.

Imam Razi presents the fifth proof for prophetic sinlessness. It is a straightforward yet powerful argument: if prophets could sin, they would fall under the same divine threats as all sinners. But the entire Muslim community agrees that prophets are above such threats. So how could they sin? This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical flow from 'if' to 'then'. Verses are used as evidence.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
The proof cites two verses: one on Hell for disobedience, one on curse for wrongdoers. See how they apply to prophets hypothetically.
3
Understand the logical structure
The argument is: if prophets sin → they are threatened with Hell and cursed. But by consensus, they are not threatened or cursed. Therefore, they do not sin.
This is a modus tollens: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
4
Appreciate the role of consensus
The proof uses the consensus of the community (ijma) that prophets are free from such threats. This consensus is taken as certain.
The consensus is considered an infallible source of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : لو صدرت المعصية عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم - لوجب أن يكونوا موعودين بعذاب جهنم ، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ﴾ [الجن: ٢٣] ولكانوا ملعونين لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَا لَعْنَةُ اللَّهِ عَلَى الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ [هود: ١٨] وبإجماع الأمة هذا باطل، فكان صدور المعصية عنهم باطلا.
The fifth proof: If disobedience occurred from the prophets – peace and blessings be upon them – they would necessarily be threatened with the punishment of Hell, because of His saying: 'And whoever disobeys God and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell' [Al-Jinn:23], and they would be cursed because of His saying: 'Unquestionably, the curse of God is upon the wrongdoers' [Hud:18]. And by consensus of the community, this is false, so the occurrence of disobedience from them is false.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This fifth proof uses Quranic threats against disobedience and wrongdoing. If prophets committed any sin, they would fall under the general threat of Hell and the curse upon wrongdoers. The Muslim community unanimously agrees that prophets are not subject to such threats and curses. Therefore, prophets cannot sin.

Key Terms
المعصية
عذاب جهنم
لعنة الله
الظالمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets might still be liable to threats for minor sins or forgetfulness.
Correction: The proof covers all disobedience; consensus affirms they are free from any threat, regardless of the sin's magnitude.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence for prophets if they disobeyed, according to the fifth proof?
A) Loss of prophethood
B) Threat of Hell and curse
C) Public humiliation
D) Exile from the community

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot sin because sin would entail divine threats that the Muslim community unanimously agrees do not apply to them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe the Prophet ﷺ was sinless. But if you were to live a single day in disobedience to the sunnah, wouldn't you be under the very threat of Hell that this lesson proves? How does this certainty change how you will approach your next decision?
?
The proof uses consensus to reject the possibility of prophets sinning. What 'consensus' of the Ummah today do you ignore when it comes to your own actions? Are you treating any sin as if it has no consequence?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah and He asks you: 'Why did you commit this sin when you knew the threat of Hell and curse?' What will you say? Write down one specific sin you will repent from right now because of this lesson.

The Sixth Proof: Prophets Practice What They Preach
Razi argues that prophets' commands necessitate their sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must be sinless based on the logical consistency between their message and their actions.

Core Idea
Prophets practice what they preach; sin would make them hypocrites.

Imam Razi presents the sixth proof for the sinlessness of prophets, rooted in the logical consistency between their message and their actions. He argues that since prophets command obedience and forbid sin, committing sin would contradict their own teaching and incur divine condemnation. This lesson explores the Quranic verses he cites and the example of Prophet Shu'ayb.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof and identify the core argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Identify the main claim Razi is making: that prophets cannot sin because they command good and forbid evil.
Notice that the proof is structured as a conditional argument.
2
Examine the Quranic verses cited
Look up the verses from As-Saff and Al-Baqarah. Understand how they condemn inconsistency between words and deeds. Reflect on why this would apply to prophets.
The verses are quoted directly in the passage.
3
Reflect on the example of Shu'ayb
Consider how Prophet Shu'ayb's declaration reinforces the proof. His statement shows that a prophet must not forbid something and then do it himself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : أنهم كانوا يأمرون بفعل الطاعات وترك المعاصي، فلو تركوا الطاعة وفعلوا المعاصي لدخلوا تحت قوله تعالى : ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ كَبُرَ مَقْتًا عِندَ اللهِ أَن تَقُولُوا مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ﴾ [الصف: ٢ - ٣]. وتحت قوله تعالى: ﴿أَتَأْمُرُونَ النَّاسَ بِالْبِرِّ وَتَنسَوْنَ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ تَتْلُونَ الْكِتَابَ أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٤٤] ومعلوم أن هذا في غاية القبح، وأيضا أخبر الله عن رسوله شعيب ببراءة نفسه فقال: ﴿وَمَا أُرِيدُ أَنْ أُخَالِفَكُمْ إِلَى مَا أَنْهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ﴾ [هود: ٨٨]
The sixth proof: They used to command the performance of acts of obedience and the abandonment of sins. So if they abandoned obedience and committed sins, they would fall under His saying: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do? Great is hatred in the sight of God that you say what you do not do' [As-Saff:2-3], and under His saying: 'Do you command righteousness to the people and forget yourselves while you recite the Scripture? Then will you not reason?' [Al-Baqarah:44]. And it is known that this is extremely repugnant. Also, God informed about His messenger Shu'ayb, who declared his own innocence, saying: 'And I do not intend to differ from you in what I forbid you from' [Hud:88].
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This sixth proof is based on the principle that prophets must be consistent in word and deed. They command obedience and forbid sin; if they themselves did the opposite, they would be condemned by the Quranic verses that criticize hypocrisy. The example of Prophet Shu'ayb shows that a prophet avoids inconsistency. Therefore, prophets cannot commit sins because it would contradict their message and invite divine condemnation.

Key Terms
الأمر بالطاعة
ترك المعاصي
المقت
براءة النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could commit minor sins as long as they don't contradict their message.
Correction: The proof shows that any sin, even minor, would make them fall under divine condemnation for inconsistency between words and deeds.

Checkpoint
What Quranic criticism would apply to prophets if they sinned while commanding obedience?
A) They would be called liars
B) They would be condemned for saying what they do not do
C) They would be accused of ignorance
D) They would lose their followers

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be sinless because their commands and prohibitions would otherwise contradict their own actions, incurring divine condemnation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself commanding righteousness to others in an area where you yourself are failing? How does the condemnation 'Why do you say what you do not do?' strike you personally? What is one specific step you will take today to align your speech with your action?
?
Prophet Shu'ayb declared, 'I do not intend to differ from you in what I forbid you from.' Is there a sin you routinely forbid others (verbally or by expectation) but permit yourself? What would it cost you to truly live the consistency of Shu'ayb?
?
The Quran warns against 'forgetting yourselves while commanding others.' In which area of your life are you most at risk of this spiritual amnesia? What concrete action will you take tonight to remember yourself and repent?
